# Kubernetes Audit Log Middleware and Backend

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement API server audit logging: the audit event creation from requests, the audit policy evaluation, the audit backend dispatch (log file vs webhook), and the audit truncation for large request/response bodies.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

    27→// Union returns an audit Backend which logs events to a set of backends. The returned
    28→// Sink implementation blocks in turn for each call to ProcessEvents.
    29→func Union(backends ...Backend) Backend {
    30→	if len(backends) == 1 {
    31→		return backends[0]
    32→	}
    33→	return union{backends}
    34→}
    35→
    36→type union struct {
    37→	backends []Backend
    38→}
    39→
    40→func (u union) ProcessEvents(events ...*auditinternal.Event) bool {
    41→	success := true
    42→	for _, backend := range u.backends {
    43→		success = backend.ProcessEvents(events...) && success
    44→	}
    45→	return success
    46→}
    47→
    48→func (u union) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error {
    49→	var funcs []func() error
    50→	for _, backend := range u.backends {
    51→		backend := backend
    52→		funcs = append(funcs, func() error {
    53→			return backend.Run(stopCh)

... (truncated)

    32→// NewPolicyRuleEvaluator creates a new policy rule evaluator.
    33→func NewPolicyRuleEvaluator(policy *audit.Policy) auditinternal.PolicyRuleEvaluator {
    34→	for i, rule := range policy.Rules {
    35→		policy.Rules[i].OmitStages = unionStages(policy.OmitStages, rule.OmitStages)
    36→	}
    37→	return &policyRuleEvaluator{*policy}
    38→}
    39→
    40→func unionStages(stageLists ...[]audit.Stage) []audit.Stage {
    41→	m := make(map[audit.Stage]bool)
    42→	for _, sl := range stageLists {
    43→		for _, s := range sl {
    44→			m[s] = true
    45→		}
    46→	}
    47→	result := make([]audit.Stage, 0, len(m))
    48→	for key := range m {
    49→		result = append(result, key)

37-assistanttool_useRead
38-usertool_resultRead
   200→func validateBackendBatchOptions(pluginName string, options AuditBatchOptions) error {
   201→	if err := validateBackendMode(pluginName, options.Mode); err != nil {
   202→		return err
   203→	}
   204→	if options.Mode != ModeBatch {
   205→		// Don't validate the unused options.
   206→		return nil
   207→	}
   208→	config := options.BatchConfig
   209→	if config.BufferSize <= 0 {
   210→		return fmt.Errorf("invalid audit batch %s buffer size %v, must be a positive number", pluginName, config.BufferSize)
   211→	}
   212→	if config.MaxBatchSize <= 0 {
   213→		return fmt.Errorf("invalid audit batch %s max batch size %v, must be a positive number", pluginName, config.MaxBatchSize)
   214→	}
   215→	if config.ThrottleEnable {
   216→		if config.ThrottleQPS <= 0 {
   217→			return fmt.Errorf("invalid audit batch %s throttle QPS %v, must be a positive number", pluginName, config.ThrottleQPS)
   218→		}
   219→		if config.ThrottleBurst <= 0 {
   220→			return fmt.Errorf("invalid audit batch %s throttle burst %v, must be a positive number", pluginName, config.ThrottleBurst)
   221→		}
   222→	}
   223→	return nil
   224→}
   225→
   226→var knownGroupVersions = []schema.GroupVersion{
   227→	auditv1.SchemeGroupVersion,
   228→}
   229→
   230→func validateGroupVersionString(groupVersion string) error {
   231→	gv, err := schema.ParseGroupVersion(groupVersion)
   232→	if err != nil {
   233→		return err
   234→	}
   235→	if !knownGroupVersion(gv) {
   236→		return fmt.Errorf("invalid group version, allowed versions are %q", knownGroupVersions)
   237→	}
   238→	if gv != auditv1.SchemeGroupVersion {
   239→		klog.Warningf("%q is deprecated and will be removed in a future release, use %q instead", gv, auditv1.SchemeGroupVersion)
   240→	}
   241→	return nil
   242→}

    28→// EventString creates a 1-line text representation of an audit event, using a subset of the
    29→// information in the event struct.
    30→func EventString(ev *auditinternal.Event) string {
    31→	username := "<none>"
    32→	groups := "<none>"
    33→	if len(ev.User.Username) > 0 {
    34→		username = ev.User.Username
    35→		if len(ev.User.Groups) > 0 {
    36→			groups = auditStringSlice(ev.User.Groups)
    37→		}
    38→	}
    39→	asuser := "<self>"
    40→	asgroups := "<lookup>"
    41→	if ev.ImpersonatedUser != nil {
    42→		asuser = ev.ImpersonatedUser.Username
    43→		if ev.ImpersonatedUser.Groups != nil {
    44→			asgroups = auditStringSlice(ev.ImpersonatedUser.Groups)
    45→		}
    46→	}
    47→
    48→	namespace := "<none>"
    49→	if ev.ObjectRef != nil && len(ev.ObjectRef.Namespace) != 0 {
    50→		namespace = ev.ObjectRef.Namespace
    51→	}
    52→
    53→	response := "<deferred>"

... (truncated)

    22→
    23→type Sink interface {
    24→	// ProcessEvents handles events. Per audit ID it might be that ProcessEvents is called up to three times.
    25→	// Errors might be logged by the sink itself. If an error should be fatal, leading to an internal
    26→	// error, ProcessEvents is supposed to panic. The event must not be mutated and is reused by the caller
    27→	// after the call returns, i.e. the sink has to make a deepcopy to keep a copy around if necessary.
    28→	// Returns true on success, may return false on error.
    29→	ProcessEvents(events ...*auditinternal.Event) bool
    30→}
    31→
    32→type Backend interface {
    33→	Sink
    34→
    35→	// Run will initialize the backend. It must not block, but may run go routines in the background. If
    36→	// stopCh is closed, it is supposed to stop them. Run will be called before the first call to ProcessEvents.
    37→	Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error
    38→
    39→	// Shutdown will synchronously shut down the backend w
... (truncated)

    35→// WithAudit is a decorator for a admission phase. It saves annotations
    36→// of attribute into the audit event. Attributes passed to the Admit and
    37→// Validate function must be instance of privateAnnotationsGetter or
    38→// AnnotationsGetter, otherwise an error is returned.
    39→func WithAudit(i Interface) Interface {
    40→	if i == nil {
    41→		return i
    42→	}
    43→	return &auditHandler{Interface: i}
    44→}

    33→// It is meant to log only failed authentication requests.

stages\\n- pkg/audit/policy/reader.go: LoadPolicyFromFile() loads and validates the audit policy from a YAML file\\n- pkg/audit/policy/util.go: Utility functions for policy matching\\n\\n## Audit implement\\n- pkg/audit/union.go: Union() function combines multiple backends into a single Backend that dispatches events to all backends\\n- pkg/server/options/audit.go: AuditOptions and ApplyTo() method orchestrate backend creation and composition\\n\\n## Audit Backends\\n\\nThree main backend types handle event persistence and dispatch:\\n\\n1. **Log File Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates a file-based audit logger\\n   - Supports both legacy (1-line text) and JSON formats\\n   - Logs events to files with rotation support via lumberjack\\n\\n2. **Webhook Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates an HTTP webhook client\\n   - Sends batches of audit events to external services\\n   - Implements retry logic with exponential backoff\\n   - Uses kubeconfig format for endpoint configuration\\n\\n3. **Buffered Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go):\\n   - NewBackend() wraps delegate backends with buffering\\n   - Batches events before forwarding to delegate\\n   - Supports throttling and async delegation\\n   - Configurable batch size and wait time\\n\\n## Audit Truncation for Large Bodies\\n\\nThe truncate backend (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) handles oversized events:\\n- NewBackend() wraps delegate backends to enforce size limits\\n- Monitors individual event size (MaxEventSize) and batch size (MaxBatchSize)\\n- Removes RequestObject and ResponseObject from events that exceed MaxEventSize\\n- Marks truncated events with audit.k8s.io/truncated=true annotation\\n- Splits batches that exceed MaxBatchSize across multiple delegate calls\\n\\n## response is written\\n\\n## Server Configuration and Lifecycle\\n\\nThe complete audit system is integrated into the API server:\\n- pkg/server/config.go: Server configuration includes AuditBackend and AuditPolicyRuleEvaluator\\n- pkg/server/genericapiserver.go: GenericAPIServer manages backend lifecycle (Run/Shutdown)\\n- pkg/server/options/audit.go: Command-line flag handling and backend initialization\\n\\nThe backend initialization chain in ApplyTo() creates policy evaluators, instantiates log and webhook backends, wraps them with buffering/truncation as configured, and combines them via Union().\\n\\n## Admission and Context Integration\\n\\n- pkg/admission/audit.go: WithAudit() wraps admission handlers to log annotations into the audit event\\n- pkg/endpoints/filters/request_deadline.go: WithRequestDeadline() handles audit for timeout-related errors\\n\\nThe audit system uses Go context to thread the AuditContext through the entire request (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates a file-based audit logger\\n   - Supports both legacy (1-line text) and JSON formats\\n   - Logs events to files with rotation support via lumberjack\\n\\n2. **Webhook Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates an HTTP webhook client\\n   - Sends batches of audit events to external services\\n   - Implements retry logic with exponential backoff\\n   - Uses kubeconfig format for endpoint configuration\\n\\n3. **Buffered Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go):\\n   - NewBackend() wraps delegate backends with buffering\\n   - Batches events before forwarding to delegate\\n   - Supports throttling and async delegation\\n   - Configurable batch size and wait time\\n\\n## Audit Truncation for Large Bodies\\n\\nThe truncate backend (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) handles oversized The main audit filter in pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go (WithAudit) evaluates the audit policy and creates audit events at multiple stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic).\\n\\nAudit event creation involves:\\n- pkg/audit/context.go: AuditContext holds the Event and RequestAuditConfig for the current request\\n- pkg/audit/request.go: Core functions LogRequestMetadata(), LogRequestObject(), LogResponseObject(), and LogImpersonatedUser() populate audit event fields from requests and responses\\n- pkg/audit/format.go: EventString() formats events in legacy text format\\n\\n## Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nPolicy evaluation is handled through the PolicyRuleEvaluator interface in pkg/audit/evaluator.go. The concrete implementation:\\n- pkg/audit/policy/checker.go: NewPolicyRuleEvaluator() and EvaluatePolicyRule() match request attributes against policy rules to determine audit level and omit stages\\n- pkg/audit/policy/reader.go: LoadPolicyFromFile() loads and validates the audit policy from a YAML file\\n- pkg/audit/policy/util.go: Utility functions for policy matching\\n\\n## Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe audit backend dispatch system supports multiple backends simultaneously through:\\n- pkg/audit/types.go: Defines the Sink and Backend interfaces that all backends must implement\\n- pkg/audit/union.go: Union() function combines multiple backends into a single Backend that dispatches events to all backends\\n- pkg/server/options/audit.go: AuditOptions and ApplyTo() method orchestrate backend creation and composition\\n\\n## Audit Backends\\n\\nThree main backend types handle event persistence and dispatch:\\n\\n1. **Log File Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates a file-based audit logger\\n   - Supports both legacy (1-line text) and JSON formats\\n   - Logs events to files with rotation support via lumberjack\\n\\n2. **Webhook Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates an HTTP webhook client\\n   - Sends batches of audit events to external services\\n   - Implements retry logic with exponential backoff\\n   - Uses kubeconfig format for endpoint configuration\\n\\n3. **Buffered Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go):\\n   - NewBackend() wraps delegate backends with buffering\\n   - Batches events before forwarding to delegate\\n   - Supports throttling and async delegation\\n   - Configurable batch size and wait time\\n\\n## Audit Truncation for Large Bodies\\n\\nThe truncate backend (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) handles oversized events:\\n- NewBackend() wraps delegate backends to enforce size limits\\n- Monitors individual event size (MaxEventSize) and batch size (MaxBatchSize)\\n- Removes RequestObject and ResponseObject from events that exceed MaxEventSize\\n- Marks truncated events with audit.k8s.io/truncated=true annotation\\n- Splits batches that exceed MaxBatchSize across multiple delegate calls\\n\\n## Request/Response Logging Integration\\n\\nRequest and response bodies are logged at handler level:\\n- pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go: LogRequestObject() during create operations\\n- response is written\\n\\n## Server Configuration and Lifecycle\\n\\nThe complete audit system is integrated into the API server:\\n- pkg/server/config.go: Server configuration includes AuditBackend and AuditPolicyRuleEvaluator\\n- pkg/server/genericapiserver.go: GenericAPIServer manages backend lifecycle (Run/Shutdown)\\n- pkg/server/options/audit.go: Command-line flag handling and backend initialization\\n\\nThe backend initialization chain in ApplyTo() creates policy evaluators, instantiates log and webhook backends, wraps them with buffering/truncation as configured, and combines them via Union().\\n\\n## Admission and Context Integration\\n\\n- pkg/admission/audit.go: WithAudit() wraps admission handlers to log annotations into the audit event\\n- pipeline, allowing any handler to access the current audit event via audit.AuditContextFrom() and audit.AuditEventFrom().\"\n}\n",

The main audit filter in pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go (WithAudit) evaluates the audit policy and creates audit events at multiple stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic).\\n\\nAudit event creation involves:\\n- pkg/audit/context.go: AuditContext holds the Event and RequestAuditConfig for the current request\\n- pkg/audit/request.go: Core functions LogRequestMetadata(), LogRequestObject(), LogResponseObject(), and LogImpersonatedUser() populate audit event fields from requests and responses\\n- pkg/audit/format.go: EventString() formats events in legacy text format\\n\\n## Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nPolicy evaluation is handled through the PolicyRuleEvaluator interface in pkg/audit/evaluator.go. The concrete implementation:\\n- pkg/audit/policy/checker.go: NewPolicyRuleEvaluator() and EvaluatePolicyRule() match request attributes against policy rules to determine audit level and omit stages\\n- pkg/audit/policy/reader.go: LoadPolicyFromFile() loads and validates the audit policy from a YAML file\\n- pkg/audit/policy/util.go: Utility functions for policy matching\\n\\n## Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe audit backend dispatch system supports multiple backends simultaneously through:\\n- pkg/audit/types.go: Defines the Sink and Backend interfaces that all backends must implement\\n- pkg/audit/union.go: Union() function combines multiple backends into a single Backend that dispatches events to all backends\\n- pkg/server/options/audit.go: AuditOptions and ApplyTo() method orchestrate backend creation and composition\\n\\n## Audit Backends\\n\\nThree main backend types handle event persistence and dispatch:\\n\\n1. **Log File Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates a file-based audit logger\\n   - Supports both legacy (1-line text) and JSON formats\\n   - Logs events to files with rotation support via lumberjack\\n\\n2. **Webhook Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates an HTTP webhook client\\n   - Sends batches of audit events to external services\\n   - Implements retry logic with exponential backoff\\n   - Uses kubeconfig format for endpoint configuration\\n\\n3. **Buffered Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go):\\n   - NewBackend() wraps delegate backends with buffering\\n   - Batches events before forwarding to delegate\\n   - Supports throttling and async delegation\\n   - Configurable batch size and wait time\\n\\n## Audit Truncation for Large Bodies\\n\\nThe truncate backend (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) handles oversized events:\\n- NewBackend() wraps delegate backends to enforce size limits\\n- Monitors individual event size (MaxEventSize) and batch size (MaxBatchSize)\\n- Removes RequestObject and ResponseObject from events that exceed MaxEventSize\\n- Marks truncated events with audit.k8s.io/truncated=true annotation\\n- Splits batches that exceed MaxBatchSize across multiple delegate calls\\n\\n## Request/Response Logging Integration\\n\\nRequest and response bodies are logged at handler level:\\n- pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go: LogRequestObject() during create operations\\n- pkg/endpoints/handlers/update.go: LogRequestObject() during update operations\\n- pkg/endpoints/handlers/delete.go: LogRequestObject() during delete operations\\n- Response objects are logged when the response is written\\n\\n## Server Configuration and Lifecycle\\n\\nThe complete audit system is integrated into the API server:\\n- pkg/server/config.go: Server configuration includes AuditBackend and AuditPolicyRuleEvaluator\\n- pkg/server/genericapiserver.go: GenericAPIServer manages backend lifecycle (Run/Shutdown)\\n- pkg/server/options/audit.go: Command-line flag handling and backend initialization\\n\\nThe backend initialization chain in ApplyTo() creates policy evaluators, instantiates log and webhook backends, wraps them with buffering/truncation as configured, and combines them via Union().\\n\\n## Admission and Context Integration\\n\\n- pkg/admission/audit.go: WithAudit() wraps admission handlers to log annotations into the audit event\\n- pkg/endpoints/filters/request_deadline.go: WithRequestDeadline() handles audit for timeout-related errors\\n\\nThe audit system uses Go context to thread the AuditContext through the entire request pipeline, allowing any handler to access the current audit event via audit.AuditContextFrom() and audit.AuditEventFrom().\"\n}\n",

through a comprehensive system spanning multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system follows a modular architecture with clear separation of concerns:\\n\\n## Core Audit Infrastructure\\n\\nThe audit event creation from requests starts with the audit context initialization in pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go via WithAuditInit(), which creates an AuditContext and generates or captures an Audit-ID. The main audit filter in pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go (WithAudit) evaluates the audit policy and creates audit events at multiple stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic).\\n\\nAudit event creation involves:\\n- pkg/audit/context.go: AuditContext holds the Event and RequestAuditConfig for the current request\\n- pkg/audit/request.go: Core functions LogRequestMetadata(), LogRequestObject(), LogResponseObject(), and LogImpersonatedUser() populate audit event fields from requests and responses\\n- pkg/audit/format.go: EventString() formats events in legacy text format\\n\\n## Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nPolicy evaluation is handled through the PolicyRuleEvaluator interface in pkg/audit/evaluator.go. The concrete implementation:\\n- pkg/audit/policy/checker.go: NewPolicyRuleEvaluator() and EvaluatePolicyRule() match request attributes against policy rules to determine audit level and omit stages\\n- pkg/audit/policy/reader.go: LoadPolicyFromFile() loads and validates the audit policy from a YAML file\\n- pkg/audit/policy/util.go: Utility functions for policy matching\\n\\n## Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe audit backend dispatch system supports multiple backends simultaneously through:\\n- pkg/audit/types.go: Defines the Sink and Backend interfaces that all backends must implement\\n- pkg/audit/union.go: Union() function combines multiple backends into a single Backend that dispatches events to all backends\\n- pkg/server/options/audit.go: AuditOptions and ApplyTo() method orchestrate backend creation and composition\\n\\n## Audit Backends\\n\\nThree main backend types handle event persistence and dispatch:\\n\\n1. **Log File Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates a file-based audit logger\\n   - Supports both legacy (1-line text) and JSON formats\\n   - Logs events to files with rotation support via lumberjack\\n\\n2. **Webhook Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go):\\n   - NewBackend() creates an HTTP webhook client\\n   - Sends batches of audit events to external services\\n   - Implements retry logic with exponential backoff\\n   - Uses kubeconfig format for endpoint configuration\\n\\n3. **Buffered Backend** (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go):\\n   - NewBackend() wraps delegate backends with buffering\\n   - Batches events before forwarding to delegate\\n   - Supports throttling and async delegation\\n   - Configurable batch size and wait time\\n\\n## Audit Truncation for Large Bodies\\n\\nThe truncate backend (pkg/audit/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) handles oversized events:\\n- NewBackend() wraps delegate backends to enforce size limits\\n- Monitors individual event size (MaxEventSize) and batch size (MaxBatchSize)\\n- Removes RequestObject and ResponseObject from events that exceed MaxEventSize\\n- Marks truncated events with audit.k8s.io/truncated=true annotation\\n- Splits batches that exceed MaxBatchSize across multiple delegate calls\\n\\n## Request/Response Logging Integration\\n\\nRequest and response bodies are logged at handler level:\\n- pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go: LogRequestObject() during create operations\\n- pkg/endpoints/handlers/update.go: LogRequestObject() during update operations\\n- pkg/endpoints/handlers/delete.go: LogRequestObject() during delete operations\\n- Response objects are logged when the response is written\\n\\n## Server Configuration and Lifecycle\\n\\nThe complete audit system is integrated into the API server:\\n- pkg/server/config.go: Server configuration includes AuditBackend and AuditPolicyRuleEvaluator\\n- pkg/server/genericapiserver.go: GenericAPIServer manages backend lifecycle (Run/Shutdown)\\n- pkg/server/options/audit.go: Command-line flag handling and backend initialization\\n\\nThe backend initialization chain in ApplyTo() creates policy evaluators, instantiates log and webhook backends, wraps them with buffering/truncation as configured, and combines them via Union().\\n\\n## Admission and Context Integration\\n\\n- pkg/admission/audit.go: WithAudit() wraps admission handlers to log annotations into the audit event\\n- pkg/endpoints/filters/request_deadline.go: WithRequestDeadline() handles audit for timeout-related errors\\n\\nThe audit system uses Go context to thread the AuditContext through the entire request pipeline, allowing any handler to access the current audit event via audit.AuditContextFrom() and audit.AuditEventFrom().\"\n}\n",

## Admission and Context Integration

- pkg/endpoints/filters/request_deadline.go: WithRequestDeadline() handles audit for timeout-related errors

After
## Admission and Context Integration

- pkg/admission/audit.go: WithAudit() wraps admission handlers to log annotations into the audit event
- pkg/endpoints/filters/request_deadline.go: WithRequestDeadline() handles audit for timeout-related errors
- pkg/endpoints/filters/authn_audit.go: WithFailedAuthenticationAudit() audits failed authentication attempts

## API Scheme Registration

The audit system's API types are registered and made available through:
- pkg/apis/audit/install/install.go: Registers audit API groups and versions with the scheme
- pkg/apis/audit/register.go: Registers the internal audit API
- pkg/apis/audit/v1/register.go: Registers the v1 audit API

The audit system uses Go context to thread the AuditContext through the entire request pipeline, allowing any handler to access the current audit event via audit.AuditContextFrom() and audit.AuditEventFrom(). Events are logged at multiple stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete) through the filter chain, with the Union backend pattern enabling simultaneous dispatch to log file and webhook backends."
